  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_72c54281-d605-480e-8aea-3c296dfb6b76'

  <span id="freeText4198516931888051527" style="display:none"><b><i>Witness the fate of beloved heroes - and enemies.</i><br /><br />THE BALANCE OF POWER HAS FINALLY TIPPED...</b><br />The precarious equilibrium among four Londons has reached its breaking point. Once brimming with the red vivacity of magic, darkness casts a shadow over the Maresh Empire, leaving a space for another London to rise.<br /><br /><b>WHO WILL CRUMBLE?</b><br />Kell - once assumed to be the last surviving <i>Antari</i> - begins to waver under the pressure of competing loyalties. And in the wake of tragedy, can Arnes survive?<br /><br /><b>WHO WILL RISE?</b><br />Lila Bard, once a commonplace - but never common - thief, has survived and flourished through a series of magical trials. But now she must learn to control the magic, before it bleeds her dry. Meanwhile, the disgraced Captain Alucard Emery of the <i>Night Spire</i> collects his crew, attempting a race against time to acquire the impossible.<br /><br /><b>WHO WILL TAKE CONTROL?</b><br />And an ancient enemy returns to claim a crown while a fallen hero tries to save a world in decay.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yep. She's been using a particular term while answering the question and saying that this is the last book for the arc. So there is a potential for mo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yep. She's been using a particular term while answering the question and saying that this is the last book for the arc. So there is a potential for more from this world but characters wise this is probably the end of this charaters. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2395258585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395258585" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395258585?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395258585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14182633593086464121"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577566310i/28681238._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Psst. A new video is up - all about the bad books I've read this year! <br/><br/>Now that you know that this one made the cut, check out the <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/c3HUZPHWlPg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Worst Books of 2019 video</a></u></b> to see what other ones made the cut! </blockquote><b>
  <u>The Actual Review</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>Rhy: </b> I messed with magic. Nearly killed everyone. Actually, it's still killing everyone.<br/><br/><b>Lila:</b> ... <br/><br/><b>Alucard:</b> Respect your limitations.<br/><b><br/>Lila: </b>...<br/><b><br/>Kell: </b>I've literally used magic my entire life and you've been at it for what, two months? This will literally kill you. <br/><br/><b>Lila:</b> That's it. I'm </span>
  <span id="freeText14182633593086464121" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577566310i/28681238._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Psst. A new video is up - all about the bad books I've read this year! <br><br>Now that you know that this one made the cut, check out the <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/c3HUZPHWlPg" rel="nofollow noopener">Worst Books of 2019 video</a></u></b> to see what other ones made the cut! </blockquote><b>
  <u>The Actual Review</u>
</b><br><br><b>Rhy: </b> I messed with magic. Nearly killed everyone. Actually, it's still killing everyone.<br><br><b>Lila:</b> ... <br><br><b>Alucard:</b> Respect your limitations.<br><b><br>Lila: </b>...<br><b><br>Kell: </b>I've literally used magic my entire life and you've been at it for what, two months? This will literally kill you. <br><br><b>Lila:</b> That's it. I'm calling mom. <br><b><br>Schwab: </b> By the power of author, I grant thee to do the ability to do anything you want sans consequences... And you are also retroactively queer because I believe in inclusivity. <br><b><br>JK Rowling: </b>*high five*<blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567353783i/28084571._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><b>
  <u>The Actual Review</u>
</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Life isn't made of choices, it's made of trades. Some are good, some are bad, but they all have a cost.”</i>
</blockquote>The Four Londons have existed (somewhat) in harmony for the past few years - but all that is<b> about to change.</b><br><br>The four realms (Black London, White London, Red London and Grey London) are like <b>alternate realities</b>, each with their own spin on magic. <br><br>They can be accessed by Antari, humans with special magic, who create doors to access the other realms. <br><br>Years ago in Black London, a piece of black magic became sentient and soon <b>infected their entire world. </b><br><br>White and Red London sealed their doors and thought they were safe.<br><br>They did not know that the creature behind Black London's downfall was still <b>alive and awaiting</b> its chance.<br><br>When Holland, an Antari from White London was sacrificed, was thrown into what was left of Black London, he was <b>unwittingly sacrificed </b>to the sentient magic. <br><br>He became subject to the whims of <b>an insane and insatiable magic. </b>For the first time, in years, black magic will walk between the Londons.<blockquote>
  <i>“Death comes for us all," said Holland evenly. "I would simply have mine mean something.” </i>
</blockquote>Meanwhile Kell and Lila must find a way to save their London, and all the Londons, before it is too late.<blockquote>
  <i>“She was a thief, a runaway, a pirate, a magician.<br>She was fierce, and powerful, and terrifying.<br>She was still a mystery.<br>And he loved her.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Talk about a <i>whirlwind!</i></b><br><br>Ultimately - this was a good third novel, though the more I think on it...the less I seem to like it. I'm going to cover - <b>what I liked</b>, <b>Tragic Hero Holland</b> and <b>Lila-gate 2019</b>.<br><br><u>
  <b>What I liked - <i>aka, I was entertained but not loving it...</i></b>
</u><br><br>It had plenty of <b>action, adventure and mayhem. </b><br><br>I legitimately did not know what direction this will take nor who would die throughout this novel. That kept it <b>fresh and exciting</b> for me.<br><br> But it did seem to play fast and loose some of the book's original magic rules... which was somewhat annoying. <br><br>Putting that aside, I did really enjoy the plot.<br><br>The way the black London magic crept across the world - crazy-cool! Plus, I liked how the "big bad" was not a traditional villain.<br><br> He had no reasoning, no logic, no overarching goal. He <b>wanted to do some bad things</b>...and he did them.<br><br>And the characters! Rhys! Oh, I was so<b> happy for him and his beau</b> - such a perfect couple. It was wonderful to have such a strong couple in the book.<br><br>I did enjoy how Lila and Kell really found their stride in this novel - the way they played off each other warmed my heart. <br><br>But... they seemed like really good friends in their banter rather than lovers. I mean Kell does say he loves her a million times... but we do not see the love develop. <br><br>However, there were a few things that took me out of the novel: <br><br><b>
  <u>Tragic Hero Holland - <i> aka, you've had a sh*tty life? Let me sh*t on it some more</i></u>
</b><br><br>By no exaggeration, the treatment of Holland was so awful that it bordered on comedy.<br><br>The guy has been to hell and back all for what? <br><br>Everyone to sh*t on him, apparently. <br><br>Kell even knew that <b>Holland had no control </b>over himself while soul-bound to the evil twins, and yet Kell let everyone make Holland's life miserable. <br><br>Kell pushed a dying Holland into Black London to die... then gets all prissy when the half-dead guy makes a deal to save his entire country. <br><br>Everyone's hatred seemed <b> nonsensical. </b>There's justified prejudice and there's over-the-top.<br><br><b>
  <i>It could be my tinfoil hat, </i>
</b> but it felt like the author was throwing the book at Holland so she could check every box from the Misunderstood Tragic Hero (TM) trope.<br><br><u>
  <b>Lila-gate 2019 - <i> aka mom plays favorites </i></b>
</u><br><br>This book was Lila's personal sandbox. She could pretty much do<b> anything she wanted</b> because "reasons"... <br><br>Logically, Lila's powers <b>should've been the weakest </b>(she's a Grey Londoner, she hasn't practiced very long, etc...) but she continuously showed everyone up. <br><br>It felt a little like the author loved Lila so much that she gave her <b>a free pass</b> to do whatever. <br><br>Plus there was the Instagram post where the author said that <b>Lila was actually nonbinary</b>... but because of the setting/time period, Lila would not have known the right words or been aware of such a thing. <blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554211788i/27304139._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>So she<i> wasn't</i>...but still<i> totally</i> was...kind of.</b><br><br>And to that I say...Excuse me? <br><br>Am I missing something? <br><br><b>Did <i>anybody </i> else pick up any hint</b> that Lila was potentially a queer character other than her deep distrust of dresses and feminine activities (which, to be honest, those really aren't true clues to anyone's gender identity)?<br><br>The author, <b>who just got done bragging</b> that Lila learned a whole new language, became a captain and forced herself to wield magic... was seemingly roadblocked from being her genderfluid self by a few vocab terms?<br><b>
  <i><br>REALLLLLLLY?</i>
</b><br><br>The girl who became<b> a magic pirate</b> couldn't grasp the concept of being gender fluid. <b>
  <i>The. Magic. Pirate. </i>
</b><br><br>Also, correct me if I'm wrong, but isn't being genderfluid more than skin deep?<br><br> As in it is the core of one's being? <br><br>As in if you truly were, <b>you'd feel it all the time</b> (or at least a feeling of something being not right/missing)... not just have <b>an AHA moment</b> once someone explains the concept (as Schwab implies).<br><br>I am of the belief that if you are going to include a character from <b>an underrepresented community</b> (especially one that is practically the underrepresented of the underrepresented communities) ...then you owe it to them to do just that...<br><br> Not just say that it would've<b>
  <i> totally happened</i>
</b> if Lila was in "X" situation but it didn't because of "Y" artistic reasons.<br><br><u>
  <b>Overall</b>
</u><br><br>This one was enjoyable. It dragged at times but picked up at the 400 pg mark. <br><br>The characters were unique and (mostly) believable. <br><br> I won't be returning for a reread but I'll definitely be checking out Schwab's other series.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Well-read, though Lila's voice did grate on my nerves sometimes.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>
  <a data-text-id="14182633593086464121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1647128687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647128687" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1647128687?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647128687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8374674919673076028">The reason I am giving this book a 2 stars is because <b>I expected so much more from both this book & this series overall and I am not very satisfied with the development or the ending.</b> Schwab had so much potential going into this series, but ultimately I find myself very let down.<br/><br/>I honestly don't know how to review this book without spoilers and so from this point on there will be unmarked spoilers for the entire series. <br/><br/><b>***SPOILER ALERT TURN BACK NOW***</b><br/><br/>I feel as though this final installment was</span>
  <span id="freeText8374674919673076028" style="display:none">The reason I am giving this book a 2 stars is because <b>I expected so much more from both this book &amp; this series overall and I am not very satisfied with the development or the ending.</b> Schwab had so much potential going into this series, but ultimately I find myself very let down.<br /><br />I honestly don't know how to review this book without spoilers and so from this point on there will be unmarked spoilers for the entire series. <br /><br /><b>***SPOILER ALERT TURN BACK NOW***</b><br /><br />I feel as though this final installment was very disjointed. <br /><br /><u>We've got:</u><br /><br />✔Perspectives tossed in here and there that ultimately amount to nothing.<br />✔Unnecessary emphasis on characters who haven't mattered at all in the first and second books.<br />✔A plot that takes almost 400 pages to really get going.<br />✔Questions raised without answers given.<br />✔A villain who feels neither scary, nor provides a real reason for his being a villain.<br /><br />So the story begins right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879.A_Gathering_of_Shadows__Shades_of_Magic___2_" title="A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> leaves off. Lila runs off to save Kell and <u>immediately kills Ojka.</u> What was the purpose of creating this neat character, giving us a glimpse of her background, just to kill her off immediately? <b>It felt rather pointless??</b><br /><br />Then we spend the next <u>almost 400 pages</u> listening to Kell brood, Alucard jab at Kell while he broods, Rhy float around from room to room (after he avoids death <i>again</i>), and being incessantly reminded that Lila is a cool chick. <br /><br />If you guys don't already know, Kell and I don't get along. I don't sympathize with his plight, and I find him unnecessarily mopey in most of his scenes (especially in the second book). <br /><br />I don't mind Alucard, but I find his character to be a bit static. Even by the end of this book, he doesn't grow into anything new and he doesn't really participate in the action scenes in a meaningful way. His sole existence in this story is to create drama for Kell, Rhy, and Lila. <br /><br />Rhy, though not one of my favorite characters, undeniably experiences the most growth of the four over the course of the book. He evolves his perspective on being given a second chance at life, and ultimately comes to understand what it means to be king. SO bravo I guess on that front?<br /><br />Lila... Ugh. I want to like Lila so much but she's basically the same Lila we met on the streets in Grey London all those pages back. <br /><br />Lila's character on her own doesn't bother me as much as the way the Schwab handles telling us about her. I got weary of reading phrases like "thief-soft footsteps" and "she was a mystery" used to describe her. Like... I get it. She's interesting &amp; capable. <b>You don't need to keep reminding me.</b><br /><br />Outside of the main cast, we get chapters devoted to random one-time characters that don't really add up to anything, and we get chapters about King Maxim &amp; Queen Emira &amp; Tieren that... don't really add up to anything. <br /><br />Throwing in perspectives like Nasi, a little girl from White London who admired Ojka, did <b>absolutely nothing</b> for the plot or the world building. This character appears two times, around page 140 and around page 520, <u>but her existence bears no consequence on the story.</u><br /><br />Using this character to explain more about Ojka's background <i>could have</i> worked, but since ultimately Ojka didn't end up mattering either it amounted to nothing more than a <b>waste of time.</b><br /><br />Adding perspectives like Ned Tuttle &amp; King George IV was <i>so incredibly boring,</i> since once again nothing of consequence happens in Grey London while this plot unfolds.<br /><br />Writing about Maxim and Emira was <i>too little, too late</i> for me. For the first two books, we've known these two to be <i>side characters.</i> This sudden shift to semi-main character status was <u>jolting.</u><br /><br />We only scratched the surfaces of the King's and Queen's lives, and there simply wasn't enough <b>there</b> for me to connect to. I felt completely unattached to them, so their eventual deaths were reduced to <u>plot devices for Rhy's development</u> instead of being meaningful on their own.<br /><br />After a huge stretch of monotony, the plot finally gets itself going when the crew arrives at the floating black market. <b>Here is where I started to become interested in where the story would go.</b> The Inheritor was an interesting solution even if its existence felt very tailored for defeating Osaron. <br /><br />For the last 200 pages I was engaged, but pretty disappointed that the resolution of the plot played out <b>exactly the way it was supposed to.</b> Hell, it played out better than it was supposed to really, seeing as Holland survived to see the plan through to completion.<br /><br /><b>No twists. No surprises. Our four main characters all survive. The end.</b><br /><br /><u>Now I'm left wondering:</u><br /><br />What about Kell's past? Sure he decided he was better off not knowing about his true parents, <b>but what about me as the reader?</b> Resolving this question with Kell deciding he doesn't need the information was <u>lazy</u> on part of the author.<br /><br />What about Lila? Where did she come from? How did an Antari originate in Grey London? How did she lose her eye, and why? <b>No, we are too busy being reassured that Lila is sly and mischievous and special to worry about her past, I suppose.</b><br /><br />How did the original tokens get into the different Londons? Can we know a little more history so that these worlds don't all feel like cardboard? <br /><br />What exactly caused Osaron to manifest into Vitari? Shouldn't we be looking for a solution to this problem since this is the second time it's happened? <b>Maybe a way to eliminate the threat that Black London poses by just existing as a magical black hole that spits out perilous villains every so often?</b><br /><br />And that brings me to Osaron himself. <i>
  <b>He just doesn't scare me.</b>
</i><br /><br />When I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>, for the first 100 or so pages I was totally and completely <i>enticed</i> by the threat that Osaron presented. His unwanted presence felt menacing and dangerous in Red London and I was intrigued. <br /><br />But by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29939230.A_Conjuring_of_Light__Shades_of_Magic___3_" title="A Conjuring of Light (Shades of Magic, #3) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conjuring of Light</a>, he's still... just possessing people? Sure, they're chanting some creepy shit. Sure, he's killed a couple unimportant side characters. <br /><br /><b>But... Is that all you got?</b><br /><br />Oh, and he creates an obsidian replica of the palace for... posturing? Intimidation? <br /><br />Once all the citizens of Red London are asleep, he's back to being a temperamental, smoke bitch until he's defeated at the end, which wraps up nicely and neatly and quickly in the last 50 or so pages of the book.<br /><br /><b>I'm not impressed by Osaron.</b><br /><br />All three of these books suffer severely from pacing issues, on both a microcosmic and macrocosmic scale. Each book begins with a slow to medium pace, then concludes in a rapid whirlwind of events <b>which is jarring to say the least.</b> <br /><br />The series takes place over the course of what, a couple months? Maybe 4? Sometimes this can work, <u>but in this case I don't feel it did.</u> <br /><br />I wish Lila had been gone for two years instead of two months. It would've made much more sense for her to come back after two years of studying with Alucard to feel confident enough to enter the <i>Essen Tasch.</i><br /><br /><b>It would've given <i>all</i> of these characters time to grow into people I cared about.</b><br /><br />Now, perhaps you noticed I have been neglecting to mention Holland.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>That's because Holland was undoubtedly the star of the show.</i>
</b><br /><br />Holland's moments were such a treat for me. I was immediately entranced by him, and I drank in every one of his stories that Schwab graced us with.<br /><br />We get his backstory. We understand his motivations. We glimpse the events that have shaped him, hardened him, softened him. <b>Holland's development causes the others' to pale by comparison.</b><br /><br />He possessed a depth I could sink my claws into. His death in the Silver Woods was beautifully tragic, and wonderfully appropriate. <b>I just wanted to wrap him in my arms and die with him.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>If this series had been about Holland, I would likely be giving it 5 stars right now.</u>
</b><br /><br />Aside from Holland, Schwab's writing once again <i>is absolutely stunning.</i> This is an author who <u>always</u> impresses me with her writing style. She is whimsical in her descriptions, unique in how she conveys emotion to her readers. <b>I am truly a fan of reading her words.</b><br /><br />But this series just did not deliver for me. I craved more intensity. I needed more unpredictability. I wanted meaningful characters that danced their way into my heart &amp; a rich world that beckoned me to keep turning the pages. <br /><br /><b>What I found here was a superb concept with a less-than-superb execution.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8374674919673076028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1845324574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845324574" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845324574?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785652448" href="/book/show/32200595-a-conjuring-of-light">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845324574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6833819497198589515"><b>As of now, this is the number one most overrated and worst trilogy that I've ever read so far.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Anoshe brought solace. And hope. And the strength to let go.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>No need for Anoshe, I don’t need any additional strength to let go of this series. Let it be known here that I won’t be reading any more books written by VE Schwab. This is where I must part way with her works. Trust me it’s better for me to do this. For her fans, I’m happy that you love her series but you don’t want to see me ran</span>
  <span id="freeText6833819497198589515" style="display:none"><b>As of now, this is the number one most overrated and worst trilogy that I've ever read so far.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Anoshe brought solace. And hope. And the strength to let go.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>No need for Anoshe, I don’t need any additional strength to let go of this series. Let it be known here that I won’t be reading any more books written by VE Schwab. This is where I must part way with her works. Trust me it’s better for me to do this. For her fans, I’m happy that you love her series but you don’t want to see me rant and rated her books with bad reviews right? I have read all her <i>(Not under Victoria Schwab)</i> book, including the novella ‘Warm Up’ and her books just degrade in quality with each new release for me.<br><br>'Vicious' being the first and the best one I read from her, it was a one hit wonder and believe me I would’ve continue with the series but the problem is, after reading this trilogy I change my mind. Vicious should’ve ended up as a standalone, it ended perfectly and I hate when authors decided to continue a standalone into a trilogy. Just like ADSOM <i>(A Darker Shade of Mediocre)</i>, the first book started and ended well as a standalone and it should’ve stayed that way.<br><br>To sum up, my experience reading this straight after AGOS <i>(A Gathering of Shit)</i>, it’s like wiping my ass with sandpaper instead of a tissue. In other word, a bloody asshole experience.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496249382i/22894378._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The plot continued straight after the previous book and I seriously thought this book would’ve been better cause it took you into the heat of the action and story right from the beginning but no, as soon as it landed on the 200 pages mark, it became so much worse. To explain this without spoiling anything, this series contained so many plot holes that a Diglett could make a living out of this series.<br><br>For example, it’s been stated from the first book that Kell lost his memory before he’s adopted into the Maresh family, just when I thought the book was going to tell his story, nope, the book said <b>“fuck you, you’re not getting one”</b> and instead, letting me know that Lila is a damned one of a kind. Apparently mentioning her Mary Sue existence repeatedly is more important than the characters background.<br><br>I’ll be honest, this book is less infuriating to read compared to AGOS because there’s less emphasis on Lila compared to before but my god this series is the first series that ever made me pray to a fictional character. I kept on praying to Kira Yagami, <b>“Kira, please write Lila’s name. Cause of death: impaled by her own knifes through her mouth.”</b> to end her life every moment she spoke.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Then why are you smiling?” “Because,” she said, “bad ideas are my favorite kind.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>OH REALLY!? How about this? Take out your favorite knifes, cut your tongue out or drown yourself in the Arnesian sea. How bowdah for a bad idea? Seems like something you'd enjoy, hmm? Hmm? HMMM!?<br><br>Apparently being reminded that she’s a badass <i>(pretty sure she literally has a bad ass now)</i> is more crucial to the explanation behind her ultimate Mary Sue developments, there is no clear explanation behind all her powers, her background, NONE! But get this, instead of Kell’s and Lila’s background, VE Schwab decided to let us know about so many side characters that barely made an appearance in the previous books. Why in the world would I care about these side characters that barely exist from before when I couldn’t even care about the main characters already? Use these pages to flesh out the background of the main characters dammit, not providing POV for so many characters that are worthless to the main story.<br><br>Like the previous book, most of the story took place only in Red London. Seriously, the amount of wasted potential on the world-building of this series too damn huge. In fact, only the first book of the trilogy applied the 4 London concepts appropriately. <br><br>The main antagonist is also one of the worst antagonists I ever read in a fantasy or any book. Not only he’s like a ghost who’s less scary than Casper, Michelin would’ve made a scarier antagonist compared to this fart, no seriously, look at this beast.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496249335ra/22894376.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The final confrontation is very underwhelming, to say the least. It took more than 500 pages to reach and it ended in less than 40 pages. Instead of a great climax scene, we receive a tedious 50 pages epilogue with cheesy romance.<br><br>Honestly, this book should’ve received a one star from me but again, I have huge praises towards Holland. This is literally the only redeeming factor of the book for me, unlike all other character, this book actually sheds light on Holland’s background beautifully. Right from his childhood up to why he’s the way he is now. <b>In my opinion, Holland should’ve been the main character of the trilogy.</b> IF every other character received the same treatment as him, this book would’ve been a much better experience. Instead all we get is brooding Kell, Mary Sue who have a fetish with knives and other worthless POV's less important than potatoes.<br><br>One last thing to mention, Rhy’s development is not bad here, in the first book he seemed like this creature that will literally fuck everything that moves, despite his stupidity in some part of the book, he actually has more personality and development compared to the Kell and Lila.<br><br>I could go on for so much longer on why this book didn’t work for me but I’ll just end it here. This series drained the energy out of me and now I’m literally exhausted. I seriously thought VE Schwab probably signed a contract with the devil or something during my time of reading this book to make this book reached its fame and praises with this quality. Don’t believe me? Look at the total number of pages of the UK edition, it’s 666.<br><br><b>Shade of Magic is easily the worst trilogy I ever read in my entire life so far.</b> It will be hard for me to ever find another series as bad as this. I know I’m on the unpopular opinion side on this trilogy here but I honestly won’t recommend this trilogy for anyone who’s an avid adult fantasy fans. I feel robbed buying the physical books and thinking this will be an adult-oriented trilogy which it definitely isn’t. This is an unpopular and honest opinion of mine, I’m glad that a lot of you love this series but sadly, it’s just not for me.<br><br><b>
  <u>Series review:</u>
</b><br><br>A Darker Shade of Magic: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845323738?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>3/5 Stars</u>
</a> <br><br>A Gathering of Shadows: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845324375?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>1/5 Stars</u>
</a><br><br>A Conjuring of Light: <b>
  <u>2/5 Stars</u>
</b><br><br>Shades of Magic: <b>
  <u>6/15 Stars</u>
</b><br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High fantasy and Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6833819497198589515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1616146050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616146050" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616146050?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30045288-a-conjuring-of-light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-villians">favorite-villians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=2017-anticipated-reads">2017-anticipated-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=top-of-the-top">top-of-the-top</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616146050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17386177003526154944">I.... don't know what to do with myself. I am so completely overwhelmed with emotions and so far past blown away... and now I'm trying to write a review for one of the greatest stories ever told.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Love and loss," he said, "are like a ship and the sea. They rise together. The more we love, the more we have to lose. But the only way to avoid loss is to avoid love. And what a sad world that would be."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>You guys... if you haven't picked up this series... start it now. As an aspiring author.</span>
  <span id="freeText17386177003526154944" style="display:none">I.... don't know what to do with myself. I am so completely overwhelmed with emotions and so far past blown away... and now I'm trying to write a review for one of the greatest stories ever told.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Love and loss," he said, "are like a ship and the sea. They rise together. The more we love, the more we have to lose. But the only way to avoid loss is to avoid love. And what a sad world that would be."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />You guys... if you haven't picked up this series... start it now. As an aspiring author... I pray to get even a sliver of Schwab or Bardugo's brilliance. The writing was absolute perfection. But really quick.. can we just focus on how freaking awesome Schwab is as a person? I don't know if you've seen her twitter... but she's so open and honest about the struggles of being a writer (not to mention hilarious) but then she pumps out something like this book. Wow. Also, I got to meet her at Yallfest. I was in a wheelchair and I couldn't have gotten back to her signing - but she actually took time to come out to me. Victoria... *virtual hug*<br /><br />Anyway, since I'm barely able to even function (I'm still a blubbering mess after finishing this book...) I'm just going to summarize a mess of words/statements below and hope it makes sense.<br /><br />Be ready because the moment you open this book... you'll hit the ground running. It picks up literally seconds where the second left off... and it doesn't slow down. The first 20-30% was non stop craziness... and it was wonderful and painful and entirely too stressful and I found myself screaming and laughing and I don't even know.. you guys... I don't even know.<br /><br />The only slow moments in this ENTIRE book were the flashbacks - and there were lots of little ones all throughout. They were very core to character development and I actually really enjoyed them. <br /><br />I literally cannot even begin to talk about the plot. I'm going to refrain from giving away any details. But I'll say this- I really liked the first book though I felt it was slow at times. I LOVED the second as it took the series to a whole new level of emotional turmoil. This one just blew me away. The pacing was perfect (as I said, VERY fast paced, only slowing during flash backs) and full of surprises (and stress). I was so attached to everyone (even the side characters) that I was literally racing through the pages so now I'm going to have to go back and reread for details. I've highlighted about 30 quotes. I've cried and laughed and screamed and now I'm completely exhausted. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"We don't choose what we are, but we choose what we do."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />To summarize, here's what you can expect.<br />1. Blood. Repeatedly. (Like... half of this book is fight scenes I feel like.)<br />2. New and interesting POVs.<br />3. Kiss your heart goodbye.<br />4. Tears. Lots.<br />5. Stress and anxiety because you'll love EVERYONE<br />6. Pirate ships. Magic. New magical abilities. <br />7. Brilliance. On every page.<br /><br />So all I have left is to sit here and proclaim my love for the cast.<br /><br />Lila is her usual BAMF self. She had so many witty one liners and she was endless entertainment. I love love loved her contribution to the story - she kinda has a character arc but kinda doesn't. She's learned to let people in, but at the same time, she's so true to herself. Some of the highlights for me were obviously moments with Kell- but also with Alucard. (Ok, brb, need to cry because of all the emotional beautifulness.) <br /><br />Kell. I literally cannot. Precious smol- must be protected at all costs. This guy. The second book made me feel for him SO much. He's so selfless that even Rhy gives him crap about being so perfect. Oh my gosh Kell and Rhy- strongest brother relationship I've ever read. I need to cry again. Also Kell and Alucard banter was EVERYTHING. And then the parental issues... you'll just have to see.<br /><br />Rhy - easily one of my all time favorite characters. He' so freaking hilarious and sassy and I feel like we would be best friends. He's easily as selfless as Kell, though he doesn't even see it. A little reckless, but he can't help it. <br /><br />HOLLAND. Holy freaking crap of the world. I did not expect to care about him so much. I can't even function right now. BYE. <br /><br />Alucard. I can't form words. BYE. <br /><br />Ugh. The whole entire cast. Even the side characters like Lenos and Hostra .. and oh my gosh the whole Maresh family... I'm just... I want to cry because every character was so beautifully done. <br /><br />The ending does not disappoint. Everything was wrapped up - and I'm just sitting here thinking... what now? What do I even do with myself? Do I pick it up and read it again? Do I sit here and grieve because its over? Ugh. <br /><br />Lastly, I HIGHLY recommend the audiobook version!! The second book and this book are narrated by Michael Kramer and Kate Reading and they are both wonderful - but especially Kate Reading for Delilah. Seriously I was LOLing so much at her sarcastic wit. <br /><br />You guys... read this series. <br /><br />OH OH is this a Leigh Bardugo / Six of Crows reference? Ahahah.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"People spoke of love as if it were an arrow. A thing that flew quick, and always found its mark."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />LAST THING SORRY. I made a playlist - check it out ;) <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://open.spotify.com/user/brilia/playlist/5wkE8flKfJMp0A7nuKVilB">https://open.spotify.com/user/brilia/...</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17224411976775416470">In case you had any doubts...<b>THIS BOOK WAS SHEER FRIKKIN PERFECTION AND I'M A DAMAGED MESS. HI.</b> I mean, how do I even review this. I don't think I really will?? I don't want to give spoilers. I just want to say <b>(a)</b> VE Schwab is a writing queen and wonder, <b>(b)</b> this is exactly what a series conclusion should be like, <b>(c)</b> i hurt man i hurt so bad in the best possible way, and <b>(d)</b> it was perfecccccccccccccctttttttt.<br/><br/><b>SMALL LIST OF THINGS I LOVE</b><br/>• Kell's coat. I'm not saying this lightly, it is literall</span>
  <span id="freeText17224411976775416470" style="display:none">In case you had any doubts...<b>THIS BOOK WAS SHEER FRIKKIN PERFECTION AND I'M A DAMAGED MESS. HI.</b> I mean, how do I even review this. I don't think I really will?? I don't want to give spoilers. I just want to say <b>(a)</b> VE Schwab is a writing queen and wonder, <b>(b)</b> this is exactly what a series conclusion should be like, <b>(c)</b> i hurt man i hurt so bad in the best possible way, and <b>(d)</b> it was perfecccccccccccccctttttttt.<br /><br /><b>SMALL LIST OF THINGS I LOVE</b><br />• Kell's coat. I'm not saying this lightly, it is literally my favourite character<br />• KELL'S COATTTTTT<br />• the romance was like A++++ and didn't overpower but yet was excellent<br />• my ships &lt;3<br />• I mean I ship myself with Kell's coat tbh but let's not talk about that<br />• magical objects. magical objects everywhere<br />• the light of my life is Kell and Alcurd bickering because they are old cranky women who don't like to share Rhy apparently<br />• Lila showing love by stabbing people<br />• sass in times of strife<br />• black magic, black magic everywhere<br />• the way the book can hurt so fiercely by damaging/taking away things the <i>characters</i> love so their pain is your pain and it's 10000 x worse than anything<br />• Holland who is a precious cinnamon muffin and should not suffer so<br />• literally me right now to Holland = &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3<br />• everything<br />• i loved everything let's just get it out there<br /><br /><br /><b>SPOILERS ABOUT THE ENDING:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Look I'm SO happy all my darlings survived but in a completely damaged way so THAT'S EXACTLY WHAT I'M HERE FOR. Like Rhy and Alcurd get to be together <i>but</i> Rhy is such a damaged rainbow sunshine of now darkness due to being 90% magic and only 10% Rhy. So it's PAIN but I'm HAPPY. And Kell can't use magic without hurting = I'm a cry wreck how are you. But he gets to see the world with Lila. Lila gets to be a pirate and...okay tbh I don't think Lila lost anything in this? She gets a ship, she gets to throw knives at Kell anytime she wants because they're in LURVE, and she gets to have adventure. <br /><br /><b>True winner of ACOL</b> = Lila<br /><br /><b>Summary of the book</b> = fucking magic<br /><br /><b>Things that made me cry:</b> HOLLAND THE PRECIOUS LAMB. &lt;3 He was so so so so <i>tired</i> and I was so so so so crying. He got to just go home and die. I mean. I can't even. I love Holland. Best antihero of them all. He didn't deserve this. But he got to be at peace.<br /><br /><b>Other Things That Made Me Cry: </b>how Rhy's father went out to die and told the guards to hold Rhy back and they had to <i>punch him to the floor to hold him back from his papa dear</i> and I just. I JUST. I can't. I think my feels unravelled right there. See??? You don't have to kill Rhy to hurt. You just kill what <i>he</i> loves and you hurt. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>BASICALLY THERE IS SO MUCH STABBING AND BLOOD AND MAGIC AND IT IS 100% EVERYTHING I LOVE IN A BOOK.</b> This is my all time favourite series omg (apart from The Raven Cycle) and it's perfect and HURTS and I've never loved characters quite as much as I love Kell and Rhy. &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3<br /><br />Also FYI: my hardcover preorder arrived <i>damaged</i> so if that's not a metaphor I don't know what is.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>"You think this is a bad idea?"<br />"Without a doubt."<br />"Then why are you smiling?"<br />"Because," she said, "bad ideas are my favourite kind."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"So Osaron is just a piece of magic with an ego?" asked Rhy.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Kell's gaze shifted to the bed, sheets rumpled where Alucurd had been lying moments before. "Taking your task seriously, I see."<br />"Quite."<br />"I told you to keep him safe, not cuddle."<br />Alucard spread his hands behind him on the sheets. "I'm more than capable of multitasking."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote> "What have you done?" demanded Kell.<br />"It was just a tonic, sir," he fumbled, "something for sleep."<br />"You <i>drugged</i> her?"<br />"It was Tieren's order," said Hastra, chastised. "He said she was mad and stubborn and no use to us dead." Hastra lowered his voice when he said this, mimciking Tieren's tone with startling accuracy.<br />"And what do you plan to do when <i>she wakes back up</i>?"<br />Hastra shranks back. "Apologise?"<br />Kell made an exasperated sound as Lila nuzzled -- actually <i>nuzzled</i> -- his shoulder.<br />"I suggest," he snapped at the young man, "you think of something better. Like an escape route."</blockquote><br /><br /><br />(My favourite quote but it might be a bit spoilery so I'll tag it)<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

  <blockquote>"And come back," added Rhy.<br />Kell paused. "Don't worry," he said. "I will. Once I've seen it."<br />"Seen what?" asked Rhy.<br />Kell smiled. "Everything.</blockquote>

<div id="review_1648452254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648452254" />
    <a title="Ashley Nuckles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55308610-ashley-nuckles"><img alt="Ashley Nuckles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570249252p2/55308610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648452254?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Nuckles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Nuckles" href="/user/show/55308610-ashley-nuckles">Ashley Nuckles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648452254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16453880697897849484">Reread January 2020: sometimes you reread a story, and you realize you’ve forgotten how absolutely fucking incredible it is. This is one of those times. <br/><br/>If A Gathering of Shadows deserved 100+ stars, A Conjuring of Light deserves 10x that many. I have no words. This series is honestly my favorite out of everything I've ever read and I just want to reread the first one now that it's all over! My heart is so happy. Anoshe ADSOM.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1382236817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1382236817" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1382236817?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1382236817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3563497260902481939"><i>“A myth without a voice is like a dandelion without a breath of wind.<br/>No way to spread the seeds.”</i><br/><br/>Victoria Schwab is my favourite. I've read every one of her books, from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10929432.The_Archived__The_Archived___1_' title='The Archived (The Archived, #1) by Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Archived</a> to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931344.The_Near_Witch__The_Near_Witch___1_' title='The Near Witch (The Near Witch, #1) by Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Near Witch</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_' title='This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Savage Song</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_' title='Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vicious</a>. Alright, not the middle grade/childrens books, but I feel like I'm a little too old for that.<br/>I love her. She is one amazing, badass author. She has such a beautiful mind, she writes the most fantastic, dark and thrilling stories. She is truly unique and I'm so excited </span>
  <span id="freeText3563497260902481939" style="display:none"><i>“A myth without a voice is like a dandelion without a breath of wind.<br />No way to spread the seeds.”</i><br /><br />Victoria Schwab is my favourite. I've read every one of her books, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10929432.The_Archived__The_Archived___1_" title="The Archived (The Archived, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">The Archived</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931344.The_Near_Witch__The_Near_Witch___1_" title="The Near Witch (The Near Witch, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">The Near Witch</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>. Alright, not the middle grade/childrens books, but I feel like I'm a little too old for that.<br />I love her. She is one amazing, badass author. She has such a beautiful mind, she writes the most fantastic, dark and thrilling stories. She is truly unique and I'm so excited what the future holds for her (and for her readers).<br /><br />It may not come as a surprise when I tell you that the <i>Shades of Magic</i> series is one of my favourites as well. The concept alone is stunning. ADSOM swept me off my feet. In AGOS I lost my heart to Rhy and Alucard (I lost it to Rhy in ADSOM already, but a heart can be lost more than once when it's Rhy).<br />I had the highest of hopes for this finale. Maybe slightly too high. I think I scared myself a little. And while I loved the book it didn't take me by storm. I think it's one of those "It isn't you, it's me!" cases because I can't find anything wrong with this book. I'm just not in love with it the way I'm in love with book 1 and 2.<br />Writing a conclusion to a series is hard. It happens so (so so so) often that I'm 100% thrilled by a series and then 100% disappointed with the last book. Only a few authors manage to make the finale as great or even better than the prequels. Two rare examples are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6896843.Nora_Sakavic" title="Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Sakavic</a>. Even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a> can't always convince me and they are two incredible writers.<br /><br />So what happened here? Why was I hesitating to pick this book up, when I was desperately pining for it for a whole year? What was I scared of? Yup, you guessed it: Disappointment.<br />In the end, the pacing was great, but some plot twists felt superfluous, unnecessary. Red London is in a state of panic and destruction. Osaron is the most powerful evil black magician ever. There is no time for anything but battle preparation. And the three most powerful magicians, the three people who are truly capable of destroying Osaron leave the country for several days? I'm not sure that's very realistic. There were several situations like this, some where I thought that they could have been left out of the book entirely and nothing would have changed except for the page count. In the end, a smaller page count and a more crafted and compromised plot would have improved the book and left me more satisfied.<br />This fantasy world also lost some of its magic. Book 1 was so special and creative, book 2 introduced us to new cultures and characters, but book 3 didn't have this original and simply magical feeling to it anymore. Something went missing along the way. Even my favourite ship (Rhylucard) was less exciting than before.<br /><br />Luckily Victoria's writing is on point. Here dialogues are simply really <i> good</i> and so is the world she created. I'm also glad that Lila finally got a grip and got off this ego trip that she was on in AGOS. She annoyed me to hell and back.<br />I couldn't give this book 5 stars even if I wanted to and 3 stars would have been the understatement of the year, but 4 stars feel just right.<br /><br />Victoria Schwab deserves a break. She is writing books like a madwoman and her books are intense and nervewracking and probably a hard piece of work for the author. And while I can't wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_" title="Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32075662.Our_Dark_Duet__Monsters_of_Verity___2_" title="Our Dark Duet (Monsters of Verity, #2) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Our Dark Duet</a> I just want to say thank you so much for the wonderful stories you share with us. You are truly awesome.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3563497260902481939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2460226925" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13519853728600312941">why on earth am i so emotional right now!?!?! its been awhile since a conclusion to a series has hit me so hard. goodness, my heart is full. <br/><br/>i loved that this picked up immediately where <i>‘a gathering of shadows’</i> left off. it was such a quick dive straight into the conclusion and this final book really has the best qualities of the previous two - more marvellous world building is at play as the characters travel beyond the city of london, and touching backstories/flashbacks are present to give ev</span>
  <span id="freeText13519853728600312941" style="display:none">why on earth am i so emotional right now!?!?! its been awhile since a conclusion to a series has hit me so hard. goodness, my heart is full. <br /><br />i loved that this picked up immediately where <i>‘a gathering of shadows’</i> left off. it was such a quick dive straight into the conclusion and this final book really has the best qualities of the previous two - more marvellous world building is at play as the characters travel beyond the city of london, and touching backstories/flashbacks are present to give even more depth and development to those characters with whom i have bonded. but where this book found its own voice was in its plot. <br /><br />this was filled with so much more action and adventure that wasnt quite as prevalent previously. so much was at stake that i couldnt put this down - i became so invested in the captivating writing, the constant peril and intrigue, and the emotions i felt for the characters and their redemption. just everything about this pulled me in and wouldnt let go. <br /><br />and even though this book hit every mark all the way through, it was really the ending that shined for me. this was wrapped up so nicely and provided the closure i needed after pouring my heart and soul into this story across three books. i felt very at peace with the way the story was resolved, which is all i could have asked for. <br /><br />and so to this series i tenderly and lovingly say, anoshe - <i>until another day.</i><br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1563416486" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563416486" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563416486?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785652448" href="/book/show/32200595-a-conjuring-of-light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563416486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11654464567958962737"><b>“Myths do not happen all at once.”</b><br/><br/>You would not be wrong in thinking of me as a girl of few certainties. <br/><br/><b>“...They do not spring forth whole into the world.”</b> <br/><br/>The usual ones: the love of my family, my love for them, and one big dream -we all have one of those, even when we don't know we do- that keeps me going.<br/><br/><b>“...They form slowly, rolled between the hands of time until their edges smooth...”</b><br/><br/>There are also one or two things peculiar to me alone, of course. Unfortunately, they have a tendency to be</span>
  <span id="freeText11654464567958962737" style="display:none"><b>“Myths do not happen all at once.”</b><br><br>You would not be wrong in thinking of me as a girl of few certainties. <br><br><b>“...They do not spring forth whole into the world.”</b> <br><br>The usual ones: the love of my family, my love for them, and one big dream -we all have one of those, even when we don't know we do- that keeps me going.<br><br><b>“...They form slowly, rolled between the hands of time until their edges smooth...”</b><br><br>There are also one or two things peculiar to me alone, of course. Unfortunately, they have a tendency to be dull things. But one of these, the brightest one, I think, is that I love stories. Always have, always will.<br><br><b>“...until the saying of the story gives enough weight to the words—to the memories—to keep them rolling on their own.”</b><br><br>And once, I used to think I knew how stories work. I thought I was able to pick them up, look them over, and tell who and what and where and when. (Though not the why; the why is always another story.) <br><br><b>“...But all stories start somewhere...”</b><br><br>I thought indeed that I could say, <i>here it starts</i>, and, <i>there it ends</i>. But as I grew, and read, I started to see that things are not quite this simple. It would take a certain story to finally make realize the truth. The truth being...<br><br><b>“...and that night, as Rhy Maresh walked through the streets of London...”</b><br><br>The truth being, stories don't like to have their boundaries set. Never have. <br><br><b>“...a new myth was taking shape.”</b><br><br>And never will.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461172204i/18834107.png" width="450" height="70" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>•One day I'll publish an essay on <b>what makes for a good storytelling</b>, and all I will write in it will be: <b>Victoria Schwab nailed it all down</b>. There is no other way to put it: <b>in <i>A Conjuring of Light</i>, and in the Shades of Magic series more generally, she was perfect</b>. Elegant, graceful, confident, composed while vibrant and stirring while unruffled, polished, dynamic, exquisite; in two words, absolutely <b>regal</b>. Schwab's prose is something you can't equal, because it's one of a kind, something you can't forget, because <i>it won't</i> let you go, and something you can't even believe, because it is, very simply, too beautiful and mesmerizing to be true.<br><br>•<b>Each one of these characters is so fleshed-out</b> I'm honestly astonished that even their <i>names</i> can stay put and flat on the page. In the previous instalment, I'd had some issues with <b>Lila</b>, who in my eyes had gone through the whole book being more boastful and hot-headed than I -or anyone- could take, instead of showing the determination and strength that had captivated me in <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i>. But the Lila we meet in this conclusion is definitely <b>more mature, while losing none of her distinctive fierceness</b> and boldness and tenacity. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“There were a hundred shades between a truth and lie, and she knew them all.”</b>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>•<b>Kell, Rhy and Alucard</b> are just as amazing as we all knew they would be, plus, prepare yourselves to be delighted -and wrecked, and shattered, and wrecked some more- by some secrets concerning Alucard's (and to a degree Rhy's) past and some crucial plot-twists determining our favourite crown prince's future. The events test them both, and they are made all the stronger by their obstacles, the ones they share as well as the ones they have to overcome alone. <b>Rhy's dedication and resolve</b>, in particular, <b>are splendidly inspirational</b>.<br><br>•It seems my stupid, stupid mind realized this only with this book, but <b>Holland is such an incredible and extraordinary character</b>. I cannot explain how much my heart bled and sang for him. I feel the need to reread the whole series just to appreciate him as he deserves and as I should have done from the beginning. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“Caring was a thing with claws. It sank them in, and didn’t let go. Caring hurt more than a knife to the leg, more than a few broken ribs, more than anything that bled or broke and healed again. Caring didn’t break you clean. It was a bone that didn’t set, a cut that wouldn’t close.”</b>
</blockquote><br>•<b>Osaron</b> is one of the best villain I've had the (dis)pleasure to meet in a long while, and I was completely caught off guard and captivated by how compelling he proved to be. Besides, I utterly adore the concept that he's pure magic. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“It is an arrogant man that thinks himself a god.<br> And an arrogant god, thought Tieren, looking to the window, that thinks himself a man.”</b>
</blockquote><br>•The plots of <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> and <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i> were already exceptional, but <i>A Conjuring of Light</i> basically <i>towers</i> over them. <b>Fast-paced</b> and <b>heart-stopping</b>, yet it never comes off as overly packed or in any way excessive -since we've already established that Schwab's trademarks are elegance and balance, I shouldn't even need to specify it.<br><br>•<b>There is one single insignificant tiny thing</b> that felt slightly random, or maybe out of place, and that's the favour that Lila traded with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maris <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I expected it to be brought up again before the end, and it wasn't, and it felt a bit like a loose end. <b>I'm really trying not to hope</b> that Schwab purposely made it so, so as to have a sort of foothold for a possible continuation/spin-off/something, I promise I'm trying, but it just seems so <i>natural</i> and <i>obvious</i> once you notice. I just don't want my heart broken (again). <br>Speaking of loose ends, I also thought Nasi's POV had been introduced because she would have a role later in the story, but that was apparently a red herring or purely a necessity in order to develop Ojka's character.<br><br>•I think that <b>plot-wise</b> this works perfectly, and I feel that this was exactly how things were supposed to go, but I was and still am dreadfully<b> curious</b> about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kell's past <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I guess that's just something I'll have to live with. (See how hard I'm trying <i>not</i> to hope?)<br><br>➽ I could try to put into words what I feel for this series, I could put my thinking cap on and make countless attempts, and still I would get nowhere. <b>There simply are no words</b>. I can only redirect you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305000667?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i></a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559469393?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i></a>, and hope they'll make my point a little clearer. Because believe me, <b>you want to pick this series up</b>. Of course, afterwards you'll want to kill me for introducing you to the most addictive obsession (?) of your life. But I'm more than confident that you'll also want to thank me. And until then, <i>anoshe</i>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11654464567958962737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8278158186151226491">Just...wow ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><i> "Because caring was a thing with claws. It sank them in, and didn't let go. Caring hurt more than a knife to the leg, more than a few broken ribs, more than anything that bled or broke, and healed again. Caring didn't break you clean. It was a bone that didn't set, a cut that wouldn't close." </i><br/><br/>What an epic trilogy this has been! That quote pretty much sums up my love for all of these characters. Dark magic has come to red London, leaving a trail of death and devastation in i</span>
  <span id="freeText8278158186151226491" style="display:none">Just...wow ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><i> "Because caring was a thing with claws. It sank them in, and didn't let go. Caring hurt more than a knife to the leg, more than a few broken ribs, more than anything that bled or broke, and healed again. Caring didn't break you clean. It was a bone that didn't set, a cut that wouldn't close." </i><br /><br />What an epic trilogy this has been! That quote pretty much sums up my love for all of these characters. Dark magic has come to red London, leaving a trail of death and devastation in its wake. Kell, Lila, Alucard, Holland and a small crew take to the high seas to find something, ANYTHING that can defeat Osaron.<br />Meanwhile Rhy (my darling love) is at the palace, trying to keep the people calm in the midst of panic and fear.<br /><br />Despite me constantly stopping and starting this book, every time I picked it back up I wondered why I put it down in the first place! So much action and drama. We learn more of Holland's background (and I learned to love him as well).<br /><br /><i> "Dawn to dusk. A fresh start. A good end." </i><br /><br />Plenty of stuff happens that I won't mention because spoilers. But this was such a wonderful round up of the trilogy, and I even got a bit emotional at the end! Love love love, and I will definitely be coming back for a reread!<br /><br /><i> "Death comes for us all...I would simply have mine mean something." </i></span>
